            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Review.  This article provides a progress report on the use of galvanic replacement for generating complex hollow nanostructures with tunable and well-controlled properties.  We begin with a brief account of the mechanistic understanding of galvanic replacement, specifically focused on its ability to engineer the properties of metal nanostructures in terms of size, compn., structure, shape, and morphol.  We then discuss a no. of important concepts involved in galvanic replacement, including the facet selectivity involved in the dissoln. and deposition of metals, the impacts of alloying and dealloying on the structure and morphol. of the final products, and methods for promoting or preventing a galvanic replacement reaction.  We also illustrate how the capability of galvanic replacement can be enhanced to fabricate nanomaterials with complex structures and/or compns. by coupling with other processes such as co-redn. and the Kirkendall effect.  Finally, we highlight the use of such novel metal nanostructures fabricated via galvanic replacement for applications ranging from catalysis to plasmonics and biomedical research, and conclude with remarks on prospective future directions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrV860bAT1guLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lipLHt3CsXcGw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsVCisb7P&amp;md5=e97b8d0130d3f5c18c77771c37670ac5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202001976"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W. H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rational Design of Sb@C@TiO<sub>2</sub> Triple-Shell Nanoboxes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2001976</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational Design of Sb@C@TiO2 Triple-Shell Nanoboxes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Ming; Liu, Yan; Zhou, Bin; Yang, Kaixuan; Tang, Jianfeng; Zhang, Ping; Zhang, Wen-Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">43</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2001976</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to its high theor. capacity and appropriate sodiation potential.  However, its practical application is severely impeded by its poor cycling stability caused by dramatic volumetric variations during sodium uptake and release processes.  Here, to circumvent this obstacle, Sb@C@TiO2 triple-shell nanoboxes (TSNBs) are synthesized through a template-engaged galvanic replacement approach.  The TSNB structure consists of an inner Sb hollow nanobox protected by a conductive carbon middle shell and a TiO2-nanosheet-constructed outer shell.  This structure offers dual protection to the inner Sb and enough room to accommodate vol. expansion, thus promoting the structural integrity of the electrode and the formation of a stable solid-electrolyte interface film.  Benefiting from the rational structural design and synergistic effects of Sb, carbon, and TiO2, the Sb@C@TiO2 electrode exhibits superior rate performance (212 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) and outstanding long-term cycling stability (193 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 4000 cycles).  Moreover, a full cell assembled with a configuration of Sb@C@TiO2//Na3(VOPO4)2F displays a high output voltage of 2.8 V and a high energy d. of 179 Wh kg-1, revealing the great promise of Sb@C@TiO2 TSNBs as the electrode in SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGreTfLplDLzwrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljatOf7byhbjQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvFWmtbjJ&amp;md5=de9e2211b9e6d06ee5f518432acb5661</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.5b13273"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Allan, P. P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tracking Sodium-Antimonide Phase Transformations in Sodium-Ion Anodes: Insights from Operando Pair Distribution Function Analysis and Solid-State NMR Spectroscopy</span>. <i>J. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>138</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2352</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2365</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jacs.5b13273</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D138%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D2352-2365%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DP.%2BK.%2BAllan%26author%3DJ.%2BM.%2BGriffin%26author%3DA.%2BDarwiche%26author%3DO.%2BJ.%2BBorkiewicz%26author%3DK.%2BM.%2BWiaderek%26author%3DK.%2BW.%2BChapman%26author%3DA.%2BJ.%2BMorris%26author%3DP.%2BJ.%2BChupas%26author%3DL.%2BMonconduit%26author%3DC.%2BP.%2BGrey%26title%3DTracking%2BSodium-Antimonide%2BPhase%2BTransformations%2Bin%2BSodium-Ion%2BAnodes%253A%2BInsights%2Bfrom%2BOperando%2BPair%2BDistribution%2BFunction%2BAnalysis%2Band%2BSolid-State%2BNMR%2BSpectroscopy%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fjacs.5b13273&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.2c09679&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fjacs.5b13273&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tracking Sodium-Antimonide Phase Transformations in Sodium-Ion Anodes: Insights from Operando Pair Distribution Function Analysis and Solid-State NMR Spectroscopy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Allan, Phoebe K.; Griffin, John M.; Darwiche, Ali; Borkiewicz, Olaf J.; Wiaderek, Kamila M.; Chapman, Karena W.; Morris, Andrew J.; Chupas, Peter J.; Monconduit, Laure; Grey, Clare P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">138</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2352-2365</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Operando pair distribution function (PDF) anal. and ex situ 23Na magic-angle spinning solid-state NMR (MAS ssNMR) spectroscopy are used to gain insight into the alloying mechanism of high-capacity antimony anodes for sodium-ion batteries.  Subtraction of the PDF of cryst. NaxSb phases from the total PDF, an approach constrained by chem. phase information gained from 23Na ssNMR in ref. to relevant model compds., identifies two previously uncharacterized intermediate species formed electrochem., a-Na3-xSb (x ≈ 0.4-0.5), a structure locally similar to cryst. Na3Sb (c-Na3Sb) but with significant nos. of sodium vacancies and a limited correlation length, and a-Na1.7Sb, a highly amorphous structure featuring some Sb-Sb bonding.  The first sodiation breaks down the cryst. antimony to form first a-Na3-xSb and, finally, cryst. Na3Sb.  Desodiation results in the formation of an electrode formed of a composite of cryst. and amorphous antimony networks.  We link the different reactivity of these networks to a series of sequential sodiation reactions manifesting as a cascade of processes obsd. in the electrochem. profile of subsequent cycles.  The amorphous network reacts at higher voltages reforming a-Na1.7Sb, then a-Na3-xSb, whereas lower potentials are required for the sodiation of cryst. antimony, which reacts to form a-Na3-xSb without the formation of a-Na1.7Sb. a-Na3-xSb is converted to cryst. Na3Sb at the end of the second discharge.  We find no evidence of formation of NaSb.  Variable temp. 23Na NMR expts. reveal significant sodium mobility within c-Na3Sb, this is a possible contributing factor to the excellent rate performance of Sb anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrDOIlQE-TmprVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljatOf7byhbjQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslKlsrs%253D&amp;md5=71511c7d7c417f4babe0b267419c0a60</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.0c02230"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Chemically Presodiated Hard Carbon Anodes with Enhanced Initial Coulombic Efficiencies for High-Energy Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">17620</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">17627</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.0c02230</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D17620-17627%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DM.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DS.%2BGuo%26author%3DB.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BShen%26author%3DX.%2BAi%26author%3DH.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.%2BQian%26title%3DChemically%2BPresodiated%2BHard%2BCarbon%2BAnodes%2Bwith%2BEnhanced%2BInitial%2BCoulombic%2BEfficiencies%2Bfor%2BHigh-Energy%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.0c02230&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.2c09679&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.0c02230&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Chemically Presodiated Hard Carbon Anodes with Enhanced Initial Coulombic Efficiencies for High-Energy Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Mengchuang; Zhang, Junyao; Guo, Shuhan; Wang, Bo; Shen, Yifei; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Qian, Jiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17620-17627</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon (HC) is an attractive anode material for low-cost and high-energy d. sodium-ion batteries (SIBs); however, its low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) limits its practical battery application.  To overcome this problem, we reported a facile strategy to compensate the irreversible capacity loss of HC anodes simply by a chem. presodiation reaction of the HC electrode with a sodiation reagent (sodium biphenyl, Na-Bp).  Benefiting from the strong sodiation ability of Na-Bp, HC anodes can be presodiated rapidly in a very short time and the presodiated HC (NaxHC) is found to have a desirable ICE of 100%.  When coupled with the Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode to build a SIB full cell, the NaxHC||Na3V2(PO4)3 cell exhibits a high ICE of ~ 95.0% and an elevated energy d. of 218 W h kg-1, which are far superior to those of the control cell using a pristine HC anode (50% ICE and 120 W h kg-1, resp.), suggesting great advantages brought about by the chem. presodiation process.  More importantly, this presodiation reaction is very mild and highly efficient and can be widely extended to a variety of Na-storage materials, offering a new route to develop high-performance Na-storage materials for practical battery applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoassfXRMz5d7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljatOf7byhbjQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXls12it7Y%253D&amp;md5=cc9cd88386f40106edcb62cafa12f284</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Voltage-Induced High-Efficient in Situ Presodiation Strategy for Sodium Ion Capacitors</span>. <i>Small Methods</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1900763</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smtd.201900763</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D1900763%26journal%3DSmall%2BMethods%26author%3DK.%2BZou%26author%3DP.%2BCai%26author%3DY.%2BTian%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DC.%2BLiu%26author%3DG.%2BZou%26author%3DH.%2BHou%26author%3DX.%2BJi%26title%3DVoltage-Induced%2BHigh-Efficient%2Bin%2BSitu%2BPresodiation%2BStrategy%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BCapacitors%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmtd.201900763&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.2c09679&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmtd.201900763&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Voltage-induced high-efficient in situ presodiation strategy for sodium ion capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou, Kangyu; Cai, Peng; Tian, Ye; Li, Jiayang; Liu, Cheng; Zou, Guoqiang; Hou, Hongshuai; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Methods</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1900763</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMMECI</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2366-9608</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion capacitors (SICs) have triggered considerable attention due to potential high energy densities under high power densities.  The presodiation process of anodes is very important for the construction of high-performance SICs; however, in the current presodiation method, metallic sodium is utilized as the presodiation agent through the assembling/disassembling of half-cells, which is very complicated and dangerous, greatly hindering the development of SICs.  Herein, a novel voltage-induced high-efficient in situ presodiation approach is successfully realized by introducing org. sodium salts as the sodium sources into the cathode.  Moreover, the irreversible electrochem. characteristic of org. sodium salts triggered by high voltage could provide sufficient sodium sources for presodiation without any neg. effects for further operation of SICs.  Significantly, the diversified anodes like carbon and TiO2 are successfully presodiated and the corresponding SICs manifest excellent electrochem. performances.  This rational strategy is anticipated to shed light on a potential avenue for greatly simplifying the assembly process of the SICs, which may largely accelerate the commercialization process of SICs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1T_85V13VKrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljatOf7byhbjQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXntl2ktr0%253D&amp;md5=087a5253c238b36157f19f0120ab1db2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201903795"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Simple Electrode-Level Chemical Presodiation Route by Solution Spraying to Improve the Energy Density of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Simple Electrode-Level Chemical Presodiation Route by Solution Spraying to Improve the Energy Density of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xiaoxiao; Tan, Yuchen; Liu, Tongchao; Wang, Wenyu; Li, Chunhao; Lu, Jun; Sun, Yongming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">29</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">50</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1903795</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The formation of a solid electrolyte interface (SEI) on the surface of a carbon anode consumes the active sodium ions from the cathode and reduces the energy d. of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, a simple electrode-level presodiation strategy by spraying a sodium naphthaline (Naph-Na) soln. onto a carbon electrode is reported, which compensates the initial sodium loss and improves the energy d. of SIBs.  After presodiation, an SEI layer is preformed on the surface of carbon anode before battery cycling.  It is shown that a large irreversible capacity of 60 mAh g-1 is replenished and 20% increase of the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency is achieved for a hard carbon anode using this presodiation strategy, and the energy d. of a Na0.9[Cu0.22Fe0.30Mn0.48]O2||carbon full cell is increased from 141 to 240 Wh kg-1 by using the presodiated carbon anode.  This simple and scalable electrode-level chem. presodiation route also shows generality and value for the presodiation of other anodes in SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsjdLCDgbkibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljatOf7byhbjQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvFersbbO&amp;md5=26d3f3492dfc8c15e83449ffb3a8e458</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1039/b922733d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Architecture of Graphdiyne Nanoscale Films</span>. <i>Chem.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We have demonstrated a methodol. to generate large area graphdiyne films with 3.61 cm2 on the surface of Cu via a cross-coupling reaction using hexaethynylbenzene.             53 other publications.
        </p><ol id="rightTab-references" class="useLabel"><li id="rightTab-ref1"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref1" class="rightTabRefNumLink">1</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit1" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202106895"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin-Based Anode Materials for Stable Sodium Storage: Progress and Perspective</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>34</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2106895</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.202106895</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin-Based Anode Materials for Stable Sodium Storage: Progress and Perspective</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xin; Lan, Xuexia; Hu, Renzong; Yao, Yu; Yu, Yan; Zhu, Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2106895</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Because of concerns regarding shortages of lithium resources and the urgent need to develop low-cost and high-efficiency energy-storage systems, research and applications of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have re-emerged in recent years.  Herein, recent advances in high-capacity Sn-based anode materials for stable SIBs are highlighted, including tin (Sn) alloys, Sn oxides, Sn sulfides, Sn selenides, Sn phosphides, and their composites.  The reaction mechanisms between Sn-based materials and sodium are clarified.  Multiphase and multiscale structural optimizations of Sn-based materials to achieve good sodium-storage performance are emphasized.  Full-cell designs using Sn-based materials as anodes and further development of Sn-based materials are discussed from a commercialization perspective.  Insights into the prepn. of future high-performance Sn-based anode materials and the construction of sodium-ion full batteries with a high energy d. and long service life are provided.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9Gn39pP64ELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhmIVNLAWjuVw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XmsFWiug%253D%253D&amp;md5=ea174905b562a0a4349fbcf3027fcf92</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1039/D1CS00948F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ether-Based Electrolytes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Soc. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>51</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4484</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4536</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D1CS00948F</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ether-based electrolytes for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Ying; Wu, Feng; Li, Yu; Liu, Mingquan; Feng, Xin; Bai, Ying; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">51</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4484-4536</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered to be strong candidates for large-scale energy storage with the benefits of cost-effectiveness and sodium abundance.  Reliable electrolytes, as ionic conductors that regulate the electrochem. reaction behavior and the nature of the interface and electrode, are indispensable in the development of advanced SIBs with high Coulombic efficiency, stable cycling performance and high rate capability.  Conventional carbonate-based electrolytes encounter numerous obstacles for their wide application in SIBs due to the formation of a dissolvable, continuous-thickening solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer and inferior stability with electrodes.  Comparatively, ether-based electrolytes (EBEs) are emerging in the secondary battery field with fascinating properties to improve the performance of batteries, esp. SIBs.  Their stable solvation structure enables highly reversible solvent-co-intercalation reactions and the formation of a thin and stable SEI.  However, although EBEs can provide more stable cycling and rapid sodiation kinetics in electrodes, benefitting from their favorable electrolyte/electrode interactions such as chem. compatibility and good wettability, their special chem. is still being investigated and puzzling.  In this review, we provide a thorough and comprehensive overview on the developmental history, fundamental characteristics, superiorities and mechanisms of EBEs, together with their advances in other battery systems.  Notably, the relation among electrolyte science, interfacial chem. and electrochem. performance is highlighted, which is of great significance for the in-depth understanding of battery chem.  Finally, future perspectives and potential directions are proposed to navigate the design and optimization of electrolytes and electrolyte/electrode interfaces for advanced batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCtrhQIYoqYLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhmIVNLAWjuVw"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony has attracted a substantial amt. of attention and has been proven to be the most promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its suitable sodium insertion plateaus and high theor. storage capacity.  However, the dramatic vol. expansion (up to 390%) during sodiation/desodiation results in severe structural deterioration and rapid capacity decay.  Herein, we report a binder-free Sb/NiSb alloy prepd. by a controllable electrodeposition process.  The inactive nickel provided both good cond. and structural reinforcement to reduce the large vol. expansion/contraction, which endowed the Sb/NiSb anode with excellent cycle stability (521 mAh·g-1 upon 100 cycles) and rate performance (above 400 mAh·g-1 at 2000 mA·g-1) that were superior to those of the bare Sb anode.  The excellent Na storage performance of the Sb/NiSb anode was attributed to the synergistic effect of its cauliflower-like structure and the alloying effect of the Sb/NiSb.  The operando XRD results indicated that the reaction mechanism resembled that of analogous transition metal antimonides.  In addn., a stable solid electrolyte interface (SEI) was obsd. with operando XRD and HR-TEM of the Sb/NiSb anode.  The cost-effective prepn. of Sb/NiSb composite anodes and their excellent electrochem. properties offer the potential to prep. a broad spectrum of binder-free metallic alloys (e.g., Bi and Sn) as high-performance anode materials for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpeg9bsSqPzG7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhmIVNLAWjuVw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVWqtrzN&amp;md5=e64989cc7cd1649fe323b9e179749800</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202000060"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Banis, M.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Polymer binders that combine active materials with conductive agents have played a crit. role in maintaining the structural integrity of phosphorus anodes with a huge vol. change upon sodiation/desodiation.  Herein, the role of binders on the structural/chem. stability of phosphorus/carbon anode is spectroscopically uncovered through unexpected mechanism.  Surprisingly, the selection of different binders is found to det. the oxidn. degree of active phosphorus in various electrodes, which correlate well with their electrochem. properties.  At a high oxidn. degree, the electrode applying a conventional poly(vinylidene difluoride) binder displays the worst electrochem. properties, while the electrode using a sodium alginate binder delivers the best electrochem. performance (a highly reversible capacity of 1064 mAh g-1 with a 90.1% capacity retention at 800 mA g-1 after 200 cycles and an outstanding rate capability of 401 mAh g-1 at 8000 mA g-1) for its negligible oxidn.  This novel discovery of the unique role of binders in phosphorus anodes, not only provides an opportunity to ameliorate their electrochem. properties, but also enables their practical applications in high-energy sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqT_PZxKYTRqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhmIVNLAWjuVw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXht1Srt73E&amp;md5=1662c6da41518e5cde975fa93816d60e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202104798"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Alloy-type anode materials are promising for sodium-ion batteries owing to their high theor. specific capacity.  However, their practical application is limited by the rapid capacity decay resulted from drastic vol. change upon sodium (Na) alloying/dealloying.  Here, a facile fabrication of well-aligned antimony tin (SbSn) alloy nanoarrays electrodeposited on copper (Cu) substrates is reported.  Such a binary alloy possesses well-defined triangular pyramid-like structure, and the subsequent thermal annealing process develops an "alloy glue" at the root of the nanoarrays which generates a strong connection between the active alloy and the copper substrate.  D. functional theory calcn. results suggest that the as-fabricated alloy offers an energetically favorable Na diffusion as compared to the individual metals, and the "alloy glue" provides a strong interaction between the substrate and SbSn.  More importantly, based on finite-element anal., such a unique construction of the triangular pyramid-like nanostructure not only creates a small difference in the Na+ concn. gradient, but also builds a uniform stress distribution that promotes both highly efficient Na+ diffusion and effective stress dissipation.  Collectively, the optimized compn. and geometry give rise to the enhanced high-rate performance and prolonged cycle life of the current SbSn alloy nanoarrays.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqav9bttQkHrbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li5mSy93HI8Sw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsVymu7nJ&amp;md5=4f7e6d18e225630b15c4cf5685caea3a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, Y.-U.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium Storage Behavior in Natural Graphite Using Ether-Based Electrolyte Systems</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports that natural graphite is capable of Na insertion and extn. with a remarkable reversibility using ether-based electrolytes.  Natural graphite (the most well-known anode material for Li-ion batteries) has been barely studied as a suitable anode for Na rechargeable batteries due to the lack of Na intercalation capability.  Herein, graphite is not only capable of Na intercalation but also exhibits outstanding performance as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  The graphite anode delivers a reversible capacity of ≈150 mA-h/g with a cycle stability for 2500 cycles, and more than 75 mA-h/g at 10 A/g despite its micrometer-size (≈100 μm).  An Na storage mechanism in graphite, where Na+-solvent co-intercalation occurs combined with partial pseudocapacitive behaviors, is shown.  It is demonstrated that the electrolyte solvent species significantly affect the electrochem. properties, not only rate capability but also redox potential.  The feasibility of graphite in a Na full cell is also confirmed in conjunction with the Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathode, delivering an energy of ≈120 W-h/kg while maintaining ≈70% of the initial capacity after 250 cycles.  This exceptional behavior of natural graphite promises new avenues for the development of cost-effective and reliable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpH2c5ZOoUcVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li5mSy93HI8Sw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFGiurrN&amp;md5=0bb4c36145b59a3b9727155eca307655</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.01.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Facile Strategy toward Sodium-Ion Batteries with Ultra-Long Cycle Life and High Initial Coulombic Efficiency: Free-Standing Porous Carbon Nanofiber Film Derived from Bacterial Cellulose</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>22</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">105</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">112</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Elucidating the Mechanism of Fast Na Storage Kinetics in Ether Electrolytes for Hard Carbon Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Ruiqi; Zheng, Lumin; Bai, Ying; Ni, Qiao; Li, Yu; Wu, Feng; Ren, Haixia; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium storage performance of a hard carbon (HC) anode in ether electrolytes exhibits a higher initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) and better rate performance compared to conventional ester electrolytes.  However, the mechanism behind faster Na storage kinetics for HC in ether electrolytes remains unclear.  Herein, a unique solvated Na+ and Na+ co-intercalation mechanism in ether electrolytes is reported using designed monodispersed HC nanospheres.  In addn., a thin solid electrolyte interphase film with a high inorg. proportion formed in an ether electrolyte is visualized by cryo transmission electron microscopy and depth-profiling XPS, which facilitates Na+ transportation, and results in a high ICE.  Furthermore, the fast solvated Na+ diffusion kinetics in ether electrolytes are also revealed via mol. dynamics simulation.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Low energy d. is the key issue that needs to be addressed for sodium ion batteries.  Antimony sulfide (Sb2S3) with high theor. capacity is considered as an ideal anode, but it suffers from poor electrochem. activity and consequently, low energy d.  Simple hollow Sb2S3 structures with high electrochem. activity offer high gravimetric energy d., while large internal voids significantly decrease the volumetric energy d.  Here, multi-shell Sb2S3 was synthesized as an anode for sodium ion batteries, exhibiting much higher reversible capacity and gravimetric energy d. than the pristine Sb2S3.  Moreover, the multi-shell structure presents higher volumetric energy d. with enhanced durability than its single-shell counterpart due to the optimized utilization of the inner void.  Operando synchrotron-based X-ray powder diffraction (XRPD) was used to verify the enhanced electrochem. activity originated from more complete conversion electrochem. reactions.                         rightTab-cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N-Doped Carbon Nanonecklaces with Encapsulated Sb as a Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jing, Wen Tao; Zhang, Ying; Gu, Yan; Zhu, Yong Fu; Yang, Chun Cheng; Jiang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Matter</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium-ion battery has shown great potential to replace the lithium-ion battery, esp. for large-scale energy-storage systems.  In this work, a hybrid material of ultra-small Sb nanoparticles encapsulated in unique N-doped carbon nanonecklace (Sb/N-CNN) has been synthesized for the first time via electrospinning and in situ substitution.  As an anode material in sodium-ion batteries, the as-fabricated Sb/N-CNN exhibits superior rate property (314 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1) and cycling stability (401 mAh g-1 after 6,000 cycles at 1 A g-1), outperforming other Sb-based materials.  Such excellent performances originate from the ingenious necklace-like structure of Sb/N-CNN, which supplies efficient electrolyte diffusion paths and more active sites for Na+ insertion/extn., disperses the stress caused by the large vol. change of Sb nanoparticles during the cycling process, and also reduces the electrode resistance.  This study provides a facile strategy for construction of a well-designed structure for advanced energy-storage technologies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo-RpsiWSBlk7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxK5GUEw2IWw"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">High-rate lithium (Li) ion batteries that can be charged in minutes and store enough energy for a 350-mi driving range are highly desired for all-elec. vehicles.  A high charging rate usually leads to sacrifices in capacity and cycling stability.  The use is reported of black phosphorus (BP) as the active anode for high-rate, high-capacity Li storage.  The formation of covalent bonds with graphitic carbon restrains edge reconstruction in layered BP particles to ensure open edges for fast Li+ entry, the coating of the covalently bonded BP-graphite particles with electrolyte-swollen polyaniline yields a stable solid-electrolyte interphase and inhibits the continuous growth of poorly conducting Li fluorides and carbonates to ensure efficient Li+ transport.  The resultant composite anode demonstrates an excellent combination of capacity, rate, and cycling endurance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr_iGAQqirQRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxK5GUEw2IWw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitVCrsbjP&amp;md5=cc3f720c4c8da9258eea0b038b7f916a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201808745"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rui, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Peering into Alloy Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Current Trends, Challenges, and Opportunities</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">One-dimensional nanotubes are very useful for achieving excellent performance in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to the fact that tubular structures can effectively alleviate the structural strain and shorten the ion diffusion length during repeated cycling.                         rightTab-cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Large-scale highly ordered Sb nanorod array anodes with high capacity and rate capability for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Liying; Xu, Yang; Wang, Chengliang; Wen, Liaoyong; Fang, Yaoguo; Mi, Yan; Zhou, Min; Zhao, Huaping; Lei, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries are a potential substitute to Li-ion batteries for energy storage devices.  However, their poor electrochem. performance, esp. capacity and rate capability, is the major bottleneck to future development.  Here we propose a performance-oriented electrode structure, which is 1D nanostructure arrays with large-scale high ordering, good vertical alignment, and large interval spacing.  Benefiting from these structural merits, a great enhancement in electrochem. performance could be achieved.  Taking Sb as an example, we firstly report large-scale highly ordered Sb nanorod arrays with uniform large interval spacing (190 nm).  In return for this electrode design, high ion accessibility, fast electron transport, and strong electrode integrity are presented here.  Used as additive- and binder-free anodes for Na-ion batteries, Sb nanorod arrays showed a high capacity of 620 mA h g-1 at the 100th cycle with a retention of 84% up to 250 cycles at 0.2 A g-1, and a superior rate capability for delivering reversible capacities of 579.7 and 557.7 mA h g-1 at 10 and 20 A g-1, resp.  A full cell coupled by a P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 cathode and a Sb nanorod array anode was also constructed, which showed good cycle performance up to 250 cycles, high rate capability up to 20 A g-1, and large energy d. up to 130 Wh kg-1.  These excellent electrochem. performances shall pave the way for developing more applications of Sb nanorod arrays in energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpRS7y0VfakjLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxK5GUEw2IWw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFGns7nO&amp;md5=50b74924c2a93cc137e8a9993ce641fa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c04366"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Durian-Inspired Design of Bismuth-Antimony Alloy Arrays for Robust Sodium Storage</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">9117</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">9124</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have attracted widespread attention for cost-effective and large-scale elec. energy storage.  However, their practical deployment has been largely retarded by the lack of choice of efficient anode materials featuring large capacity and electrochem. stability and robustness.  Herein, we report a durian-inspired design and template-free fabrication of a robust sodium anode based on triangular pyramid arrays of Bi0.75Sb0.25 alloy electrodeposited on Cu substrates.  The Bi0.75Sb0.25 arrays exhibit an appreciable electrochem. robustness for sodium storage, sustaining a reversible capability 335 mAh g-1 at a high rate of 2.5 A g-1 and 87% of the initial capacity over 2000 cycles.  We further demonstrate the applicability of the Bi0.75Sb0.25 array anode in sodium full cells by pairing it with a Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode. A high capacity of 318.4 mAh g-1 is obtained at 0.08 A g-1, and a capacity retention of 98.5% is also maintained after 200 cycles at 0.8 A g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultrathin few-layer materials have attracted intensive research attention because of their distinctive and unique properties.  Few-layer GeP (FL-GP) is potentially interesting for application in electronics and optoelectronics because of its appropriate band gap and good stability under ambient conditions.  Nevertheless, it is a challenge to achieve ultrathin few-layer or single layer GeP from exfoliation of bulk crystals.  Here, a lithiation-assisted chem. exfoliation technique is employed to achieve FL-GP, in which the interlayer spacing can be efficiently enlarged after a preliminary lithium ion intercalation, allowing the bulk crystal to be readily exfoliated in a following ultrasonication.  As a result, ultrathin FL-GP is obtained.  In a demonstration, the FL-GP/reduced graphene oxide (rGO) demonstrates remarkable sodium storage performance.  The FL-GP with a two-dimensional structure shortens the ion transport pathways and alleviates the vol. variation during sodiation.  Meanwhile, the rGO in the composite improves the cond. of the whole electrode.  The as-prepd. FL-GP/rGO electrode exhibits a high capacity of 504.2 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, remarkable rate performance, and superior cycling stability in the half cells.  FL-GP/rGO//Na3V2(PO4)3 full cells are also assembled and demonstrated satisfactory electrochem. performance, indicating potential application of the as-prepd. anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWzf_CyI5KwrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ligiLqS5OOYPg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXjvFKmsrw%253D&amp;md5=4375e497a01cdb0200b1dd9dee0008b2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c00366"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is regarded as an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  Combining Sb with carbonaceous materials has been considered as an effective way to resolve the serious vol. expansion issues.  Sb/C composites mainly consist of two types, i.e., Sb confined inside a carbon matrix and Sb deposited on the surface of a carbon matrix, and both have shown superior sodium storage performance.  However, which structure is more beneficial for achieving high electrochem. performance is still unclear.  In this work, peapod-like Sb@C and corn-like C@Sb nanotubes are synthesized via a nanoconfined galvanic replacement reaction and used as model materials for sodium storage to explore the above issue.  When evaluated as anode materials for SIBs, the peapod-like Sb@C shows a higher rate capability and a significantly better long-term cycling stability compared to those of the corn-like C@Sb.  Electrochem. anal. reveals that the peapod-like Sb@C exhibits faster Na+ and electron transport kinetics and higher proportions of surface capacitive contributions.  These results demonstrate the structural superiority of the nanoconfined structure and provide valuable information for the rational design and construction of Sb-based anode materials for high-performance electrochem. energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoffTaOrNgQZrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ligiLqS5OOYPg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXnslehsrw%253D&amp;md5=17554b3d1ee580321731a053ddf5e39c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE01501H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading which is largely due to the large vol. expansion during sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at the nanoscale or using carbonaceous materials as the buffer layer is essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile carbon-coating coupled with a thermal-redn. strategy has been developed to synthesize unique Sb@C coaxial nanotubes.  With different annealing time, the hollow space and the amt. of Sb inside the tube can be easily tuned by the partial evapn. of Sb.  The as-obtained Sb@C nanotubes exhibit excellent sodium storage properties.  The remarkable electrochem. performance results from the unique coaxial nanoarchitecture.  Specifically, it delivers a high specific capacity of 407 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 240 cycles.  Furthermore, a stable capacity of 240 mAh g-1 can be retained at 1.0 A g-1 even after 2000 cycles.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bi was demonstrated as a promising anode for Na-ion batteries (NIBs) because it has high gravimetry (386 mA-h g-1) and volumetric capacity (3800 mA-h cm-3).  However, Bi suffers from large vol. expansion during sodiation, leading to poor electrochem. performance.  The construction of a nanostructure with sufficient void space to accommodate the vol. change was proven effective for achieving prolonged cycling stability.  However the excessive void space will definitely decrease the volumetric energy d. of the battery.  Herein, the authors design optimized Bi@Void@C nanospheres (Bi@Void@C-2) with yolk-shell structure that exhibit the best cycling performance and enhanced volumetric energy d.  The optimized void space not only could buffer the vol. change of the Bi nanosphere but also could keep the high volumetric energy d. of the battery.  The Bi@Void@C-2 shows an excellent rate capacity of 173 mA-h g-1 at ultrahigh c.d. of 100 A g-1 and long-cycle life (198 mA-h g-1 at 20 A g-1 over 10,000 cycles).  The origin of the superior performance is achieved through in-depth fundamental studies during battery operation using in situ XRD and in situ transmission electron microscope (TEM), complemented by theor. calcns. and ex situ TEM observation.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal phosphides are regarded as promising anode candidates for high-energy-d. potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) due to their high theor. capacity and relatively low operation voltage.  The failure mechanism of the metal phosphides originates from the large vol. variation during cycling, which leads to fast capacity degrdn.  Herein, concd. electrolyte is used to achieve impressive cycling stability for K-metal and K-ion batteries over their more dil. counterparts, mainly benefiting from the anion-derived robust and uniform solid-electrolyte interphase layer, which is helpful in maintaining the electrode integrity, avoiding excessive side reactions, and suppressing electrolyte decompn.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphynes (GYs) are carbon allotropes with single-atom thickness that feature layered 2D structure assembled by carbon atoms with sp- and sp2- hybridization form.  Various functional theories have predicted GYs to have natural band gap with Dirac cones structure, presumably originating from inhomogeneous π-bonding between those carbon atoms with different hybridization and overlap of the carbon 2pz orbitals.  Among all the GYs, graphdiyne (GDY) was the first reported to be prepd. practically and, hence, attracted the attention of many researchers toward this new planar, layered material, as well as other GYs.  Several approaches have been reported to be able to modify the band gap of GDY, contg. invoking strain, boron/nitrogen doping, nanoribbon architectures, hydrogenation, and so on.  GDY has been well-prepd. in many different morphologies, like nanowires, nanotube arrays, nanowalls, nanosheets, ordered stripe arrays, and 3D framwork.  The fascinating structure and electronic properties of GDY make it a potential candidate carbon material with many applications.  It has recently revealed the practicality of GDY as catalyst; in rechargeable batteries, solar cells, electronic devices, magnetism, detector, biomedicine, and therapy; and for gas sepn. as well as water purifn.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8B3UhRrzmrLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljM0grMYIkVFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlyiu73F&amp;md5=5355dfb85e56c2056a3a9700829ad63c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1039/C8CS00773J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphdiyne: Synthesis, Properties, and Applications</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphdiyne (GDY), a new two-dimensional (2D) carbon allotrope, has been receiving increased attention.  Its unique sp-sp2 carbon atoms, uniform pores, and highly π-conjugated structure provide promising potential in practical applications, such as gas sepn., catalysis, water remediation, humidity sensor, and energy-related fields.  In the recent years, considerable efforts have been expended toward the development of well-defined GDY.  However, GDY materials still face numerous challenges, including the need for a more thorough understanding of the growth mechanism, strategies for synthesizing one- or few-layer single-cryst. GDY films, characterization of basic physicochem. properties, and achievement of promising applications.  This review aims at providing a comprehensive update on the synthesis of GDY and GDY-based materials, as well as their properties, including structural, electronic, mech., and spectral properties, and their applications in nanotechnol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpHRgzWSx-MHLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljM0grMYIkVFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjsVamuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=6e2e1ea887cdcd6e056c9f67fe027e91</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201711366"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zuo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrathin Graphdiyne Nanosheets Grown in Situ on Copper Nanowires and Their Performance as Lithium-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Angew.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphdiyne (GDY), a novel large π-conjugated carbon material, for the first time, is introduced as the hole transfer layer into a photoelectrochem. water splitting cell (PEC).         </div><div class="casAbstract">In the current research project, we have prepd. a novel Sb@C nanosphere anode with biomimetic yolk-shell structure for Li/Na-ion batteries via a nanoconfined galvanic replacement route.  The yolk-shell microstructure consists of Sb hollow yolk completely protected by a well-conductive carbon thin shell.  The substantial void space in the these hollow Sb@C yolk-shell particles allows for the full vol. expansion of inner Sb while maintaining the framework of the Sb@C anode and developing a stable SEI film on the outside carbon shell.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Review.  This article provides a progress report on the use of galvanic replacement for generating complex hollow nanostructures with tunable and well-controlled properties.  We begin with a brief account of the mechanistic understanding of galvanic replacement, specifically focused on its ability to engineer the properties of metal nanostructures in terms of size, compn., structure, shape, and morphol.  We then discuss a no. of important concepts involved in galvanic replacement, including the facet selectivity involved in the dissoln. and deposition of metals, the impacts of alloying and dealloying on the structure and morphol. of the final products, and methods for promoting or preventing a galvanic replacement reaction.  We also illustrate how the capability of galvanic replacement can be enhanced to fabricate nanomaterials with complex structures and/or compns. by coupling with other processes such as co-redn. and the Kirkendall effect.  Finally, we highlight the use of such novel metal nanostructures fabricated via galvanic replacement for applications ranging from catalysis to plasmonics and biomedical research, and conclude with remarks on prospective future directions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrV860bAT1guLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj45mNs79JAog"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsVCisb7P&amp;md5=e97b8d0130d3f5c18c77771c37670ac5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref48" class="rightTabRefNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit48" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202001976"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to its high theor. capacity and appropriate sodiation potential.  However, its practical application is severely impeded by its poor cycling stability caused by dramatic volumetric variations during sodium uptake and release processes.  Here, to circumvent this obstacle, Sb@C@TiO2 triple-shell nanoboxes (TSNBs) are synthesized through a template-engaged galvanic replacement approach.  The TSNB structure consists of an inner Sb hollow nanobox protected by a conductive carbon middle shell and a TiO2-nanosheet-constructed outer shell.  This structure offers dual protection to the inner Sb and enough room to accommodate vol. expansion, thus promoting the structural integrity of the electrode and the formation of a stable solid-electrolyte interface film.  Benefiting from the rational structural design and synergistic effects of Sb, carbon, and TiO2, the Sb@C@TiO2 electrode exhibits superior rate performance (212 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) and outstanding long-term cycling stability (193 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 4000 cycles).  Moreover, a full cell assembled with a configuration of Sb@C@TiO2//Na3(VOPO4)2F displays a high output voltage of 2.8 V and a high energy d. of 179 Wh kg-1, revealing the great promise of Sb@C@TiO2 TSNBs as the electrode in SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGreTfLplDLzwrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAk99RXQGgnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvFWmtbjJ&amp;md5=de9e2211b9e6d06ee5f518432acb5661</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref49" class="rightTabRefNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit49" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.5b13273"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Allan, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Operando pair distribution function (PDF) anal. and ex situ 23Na magic-angle spinning solid-state NMR (MAS ssNMR) spectroscopy are used to gain insight into the alloying mechanism of high-capacity antimony anodes for sodium-ion batteries.  Subtraction of the PDF of cryst. NaxSb phases from the total PDF, an approach constrained by chem. phase information gained from 23Na ssNMR in ref. to relevant model compds., identifies two previously uncharacterized intermediate species formed electrochem., a-Na3-xSb (x ≈ 0.4-0.5), a structure locally similar to cryst. Na3Sb (c-Na3Sb) but with significant nos. of sodium vacancies and a limited correlation length, and a-Na1.7Sb, a highly amorphous structure featuring some Sb-Sb bonding.  The first sodiation breaks down the cryst. antimony to form first a-Na3-xSb and, finally, cryst. Na3Sb.  Desodiation results in the formation of an electrode formed of a composite of cryst. and amorphous antimony networks.  We link the different reactivity of these networks to a series of sequential sodiation reactions manifesting as a cascade of processes obsd. in the electrochem. profile of subsequent cycles.  The amorphous network reacts at higher voltages reforming a-Na1.7Sb, then a-Na3-xSb, whereas lower potentials are required for the sodiation of cryst. antimony, which reacts to form a-Na3-xSb without the formation of a-Na1.7Sb. a-Na3-xSb is converted to cryst. Na3Sb at the end of the second discharge.  We find no evidence of formation of NaSb.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon (HC) is an attractive anode material for low-cost and high-energy d. sodium-ion batteries (SIBs); however, its low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) limits its practical battery application.  To overcome this problem, we reported a facile strategy to compensate the irreversible capacity loss of HC anodes simply by a chem. presodiation reaction of the HC electrode with a sodiation reagent (sodium biphenyl, Na-Bp).  Benefiting from the strong sodiation ability of Na-Bp, HC anodes can be presodiated rapidly in a very short time and the presodiated HC (NaxHC) is found to have a desirable ICE of 100%.  When coupled with the Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode to build a SIB full cell, the NaxHC||Na3V2(PO4)3 cell exhibits a high ICE of ~ 95.0% and an elevated energy d. of 218 W h kg-1, which are far superior to those of the control cell using a pristine HC anode (50% ICE and 120 W h kg-1, resp.), suggesting great advantages brought about by the chem. presodiation process.  More importantly, this presodiation reaction is very mild and highly efficient and can be widely extended to a variety of Na-storage materials, offering a new route to develop high-performance Na-storage materials for practical battery applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoassfXRMz5d7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAk99RXQGgnQ"> &gt;&gt;
